BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS OF COOK COUNTY
COMMISSIONERS
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, air pollution has been shown to be a contributing factor to premature death, aggravating
asthma and is especially harmful to vulnerable groups such as children, the elderly and people with
existing lung and heart disease; and
WHEREAS, the United States Environmental Protection Agency has ruled that the Chicago metropolitan
area is a severe non-attainment area for ozone and failure to conform with the U.S. Environmental
Protection Agency Clean Air Act standards; and
WHEREAS, non-attainment area status could lead to a loss of federal transportation dollars, the
curtailment of economic opportunities and the imposition of other federal sanctions that could erode local
control for the Chicago metropolitan area; and
WHEREAS, the twenty-five coal-fired power plants in Illinois are a significant source of air pollution in
Illinois, emitting smog-forming nitrogen oxides, sulfur dioxide contributing to particulate pollution and
carbon dioxide contributing to climate change and toxic metals; and

1912

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 200 I

WHEREAS, the coal-fired power plants of Illinois were built between 1951 and 1975 making them
exempt from meeting the pollution standards of the Clean Air Act; and
WHEREAS, pollution from coal-fired power plants could be reduced by installing modern pollution
controls or burning cleaner fuel s such as natural gas; and
WHEREAS, there is a threat to the health and safety of the residents of Cook County and the State of
Illinois because of the emissions from the coal-fired power plants.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the Board
does hereby urge Governor George Ryan and the Illinois General Assembly to ensure that pollution from
coal-fired power plants be dramatically reduced by passing legislation that would effectively end the
"grandfathering" of these plants from the new plant emission standards of the Clean Air Act; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be presented to Governor
George Ryan and the Illinois General Assembly.

This item was WITHDRAWN from the consent calendar and placed on the New Items Agenda with a
Co-Sponsor.

* * * * *

WILLIAM R. MORAN, County Commissioner

PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, air pollution has been shown to be a contributing factor to premature death, aggravating
asthma and is especially hannful to vulnerable groups such as children, the elderly and people with
existing lung and heart disease; and
WHEREAS, the United States Environmental Protection Agency has ruled that the Chicago metropolitan
area is a severe non-attainment area for ozone and failure to conform with the U.S. Environmental
Protection Agency Clean Air Act standards; and
WHEREAS, non-attainment area status could lead to a loss of federal transportation dollars, the
curtailment of economic opportunities and the imposition of other federal sanctions that could erode local
control for the Chicago metropolitan area; and
WHEREAS, the twenty-five coal-fired power plants in Illinois are a significant source of air pollution in
Illinois, emitting smog-forming nitrogen oxides, sulfur dioxide contributing to particulate pollution and
carbon dioxide contributing to climate change and toxic metals; and
WHEREAS, the coal-fired power plants of Illinois were built between 1951 and 1975 making them
exempt from meeting the pollution standards of the Clean Air Act; and

1913

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001

WHEREAS, pollution from coal-fired power plants could be reduced by installing modern pollution
controls or burning cleaner fuels such as natural gas; and
WHEREAS, there is a threat to the health and safety of the residents of Cook County and the State of
Illinois because of the emissions from the coal-fired power plants.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the
Board does hereby urge Governor George Ryan and the Illinois General Assembly to ensure that

Air Act; and

may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

referred to the Committee on Environmental Control. (Comm. No. 244064). The motion carried
unanimously.

BUREAU OF ADMINISTRATION - CHIEF ADMINISTRATIVE OFFICER
TRAVEL REIMBURSEMENT
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 17, 2001 from
JAMES L. ELDRIDGE, JR., Chief Administrative Officer, Bureau of Administration
Requesting that Section I, Paragraph (A), of the Cook County Travel and Transportation Expense
Reimbursement Plan be amended as follows:
A.

Any employee who is required and authorized to use his/her personally owned automobile on
conduct of official County business shall be allowed and paid semi-monthly compensation.
The number of County business miles driven per 112 month will be compensated at the
standard IRS deduction for business related transportation currently in effect and authorized
by the Bureau of Administration. IRS mileage rates adjusted midyear will not be made
retroactive. The current I RS mileage rate in effect is $.345.

The Internal Revenue Service has increased the allowable standard business reimbursement for mileage
from $.325 to $.345. Effective June I, 2001, any employee who is required and authorized to use his/her
personally owned automobile in the conduct of official County business shall be compensated at $.345
per mile. No retroactive reimbursement will be allowed before the June I date.
The increase in reimbursements for employees covered under separate collective bargaining or union
agreements shall be effective as stated in each separate contract.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Chief
Administrative Officer be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

1914

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001

OFFICE OF THE COUNTY ASSESSOR
CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated June 5, 2001 from
M. VERONICA LYNCH, Chief Deputy Assessor
requesting authori zation for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Larco International,
Cicero, Ill inois, to create, mail and process the application, in a bi-lingual fo rmat, for the Homeowner
Exemption for Long-Term Properties Ordinance.
Reason:

The Homeowner Exemption for Long-Term Properties (HELP) Ordinance was approved by
the Board of Commissioners earlier today. As the first step, HELP requi red the Assessor's
Office to administer the application and qualification process.
As Chairman Daley and Commissioner Lechowicz indicated at the Finance Committee
hearing, implementation of the program would req uire additional financial means for our
office to handle the req uirements of the program in time for the 200 1 tax bills. I have
reviewed the requirements of the ordinance and identified the budget and sched ul ing
considerations for this program.
At the current stage of the tax bill process, it is imperative that the required program
applications be mailed to identifiable homeowners and returned to the Assessor's Office no
later than July 9. Also, unlike the homeowners exemption, which merely requires a verifying
signature of the homeowner, HELP, as currently amended, will requ ire that owners provide
information verifying household income. In order to maintain the integrity of the program,
this process requires manual review of income statements by my office along with accessible
space for annual income documentation.
C urrently the Assessor's Office does not possess the staff to complete these tas ks within the
ordained time parameters. Therefore, the Assessor recommends that for th is first year of the
program both the mailing and processing be contracted as a sole source to the vendor who has
been the low bidder for each of the four major ma il and mai l processing jobs undertaken by
our office. The recommended vendor is Larco International, 3250 South Central A venue,
C icero, Illinois 60804.

Estimated Fiscal lmpact: $ 109,000.00. One time purchase. ( 490-260 Account).

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to suspend the ru les so that th is matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commiss ioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

PROPOSED CONTRACT AMENDMENT

Transmitting a Communication, dated May 25, 2001 from
TERRY A. STECZO, Deputy Assessor for Administration &Taxpayer Services
Re:

Assigmnent of Contract No. 99-43-1256

The Assessor's Office requests approval of assignment of the above contract from Xpedior, Inc., Chicago,
Illinois, to Risetime, Inc., Chicago, Illinois, and authorization for the Purchasing Agent to execute the
Consent to Assignment. Assigmnent of the contract to Risetime, Inc., is the most efficient and effective
means to complete the Automation Plan for the Assessor's Office. We have conferred and worked with
the State's Attorney's Office on all aspects of this transaction.
The Chief lnformation Officer has reviewed this item and concurs with this recommendation.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Deputy
Assessor for Administration & Taxpayer Services be approved. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Collins, moved to defer consideration of the contract
amendment to the June 19, 200 I Board meeting. The motion carried unanimously.

Permit#:

010318
$10,060.00

This request is pursuant to the County Board's adoption of ltem No. 176427 on September 16, 1991 that
all building and zoning permit fees be waived for public entities defined as county, township,
municipality, municipal corporation, school district, forest preserve district, park district, fire protection
district, sanitary district, library district and all other local governmental bodies.

OFFICE OF THE CLERK OF THE CIRCUIT COURT
CONTRACT ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 24, 200 I from
DOROTHY BROWN, Clerk of the Circuit Court
In accordance with 705 ILCS I 05/27.8(a), an a udit of the Clerk of the Circuit Court is to be performed
and completed within six months after the County's fi scal year end. Although s ignificant progress has
been made on the FY2000 audit, the auditors do not expect to have the final audit report completed by the
due date, May 3 1, 2001 .
Therefore, I respectfully request the Cook County Board of Commissioners approve a six-month
extension of the due date as allowed by Illinois State Statute.
Extension period: June 1, 200 I through November 30, 200 I.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Carr, moved that the request of the C lerk of the Circuit
Court be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

1921

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
GRANT A WARD RENEWAL
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 15, 2001 from
CHARLES F. LAGGES, Director, Department of Environmental Control
requesting authorization and approval to renew a grant award in the amount of $272, 180.00 from the
United States Environmental Protection Agency.
The purpose of this grant is to provide supplementa l funding for the continued operation and maintenance
of specialized air pollution monitoring sites in Cook County sites pursuant to the Illinoi s Environmental
Protection Agency Air Monitoring Plan fo r 200 1-02. These sites measure the 2.5 micron-sized partic les
suspended in the air as part of a new requirement from the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency and are
part of a special research project to determine the quantity and composition of these very small particles
in the urban air.
The grant does not require any matching fund s from Cook County.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $272, 180.00. Funding period: March I, 200 I through
February 28, 2002.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Director of
the Department of Environmental Control be approved and that the Proper Officials be authori zed to sign
on behalf of Cook County. The motion carried unanimous ly.

WALLY S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Sale of Highway Maintenance Equipment
Twenty-Nine (29) Units Lot Purchase
Account No. 001-51-05 Revenue
Fiscal Impact: $48,000.00
The Bureau of Maintenance of the Highway Department is making an effort to reduce operating costs and
downsize the fleet of road maintenance equipment. It is necessary and beneficial to dispose of certain
expendable equipment by lot purchase, no partial bids. The equipment proposed to be sold is antiquated
and expensive to maintain or reached the end of its useful life.
The intent of disposal and logistics for the sale of this equipment will be prepared by the Highway
Department to assist the Purchasing Agent in the preparation of this used equipment sale. The Forest
Preserve District was provided the opportunity to view and take possession of any equipment prior to this
sale.

WHEREAS, the County Board has adopted a Resolution stating that the public interest requires the

Department that the County Highway be constructed and improved by law; and
WHEREAS, the Department did consider the desirability and importance of the proposed improvement
and determined that the construction will be practically possible; and
WHEREAS, the Department determined that the improvement will be of public utility and convenience
and after such consideration certified its approval of the proposed improvement to the Cook County
Board of Commissioners; and

be prepared proper surveys, maps, plans, specifications and estimates of cost of the proposed
improvement; and

1935

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001

submitted herewith.

is authorized and directed to do any and all acts necessary and proper for the acquisition of the property

CONTRACTS
Transm itting a Communication from
DONALD P. O' CONNELL, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authori zation for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with REALE Consultants,
Chicago, Illinois, for professional services for the Adult Probation Department, Circuit Court of Cook
County . These services will be provided by Dr. Arthur J. Luri gio, President of REALE Consultants.
Reason :

Dr. Lurigio will analyze and evaluate current department practices and programs relating to
females on probation and pretrial supervision. Dr. Lurigio will conduct interviews with
female probationers and probation officers, evaluate the department's programs for female
offenders, and assess community-based services available to females in Cook County. The
work to be performed by Dr. Lurigio wi ll help improve gender responsive programming for
the growing population of female offenders in Cook County.
In addition to his position with REALE Consultants, Dr. Lurigio is a professor and
chairperson of the Crim inal Justice Department at Loyola University Chicago. His 17 years
of experience with the Adult Probation Department as the Director for Research and
Evaluation, as well as his extensive research relating to female offenders, uniquely qualifies
him for this project. Also, Dr. Lurigio has written a study of female gang members and HIV
prevention programs for female offenders, and served as the principal investigator for the
ROOTS project, a drug treatment program for females in the Department of Corrections.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $60,000.00. Contract period: June I, 200 I through August 3 1, 2002. (532-260
Account). Requisition No. 15321454.

Transmitting a Communication from
DONNA L. DUNNINGS, Interim Director, Department of Risk Management
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew the contract with AON to administer the
County' s optional universal life program with American General Life Insurance Company. There is no
direct fiscal impact to Cook County as all compensation will be paid I 00% from payroll deduction
contributions for this program.
This program has been in effect s ince 1986. Approximately 8,000 employees are currently enrolled. The
American General Insurance Company will be providing an improved product and more efficient
administration process for this upcoming term.
The Universal Life product provides cash value life insurance coverage to our employees on a guaranteed
issue basis (no medical questions). Employees will be able to purchase limits of up to $250,000.00 by
payroll deduction. This extension will allow for employees to receive access to this benefit.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Contract period: June 15, 2001 through March 14, 2002.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to renew the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE SHERIFF
AGREEMENT ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 22, 2001 from
MICHAEL F. SHEAHAN, Sheriff of Cook County
by
CARMELITA WAGNER, Executive Director of Community Based Programs
requesting authorization to accept a supplemental grant/co-op agreement in the amount of$ I 92,432.00
from the United States Department of T reasury, Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco and Firearms (ATF) and
extend from August I, 200 I through January 15, 2002.
The purpose of the increase and extension is to continue operation of the gang prevention program known
as Gang Resistance Education and Training (G.R.E.A.T.).
G.R.E.A.T. is a program designed to decrease gang violence across the nation which utilizes the skills of
the ATF, state and local law enforcement personnel to administer the elementary school curriculum.
G.R.E.A.T. students are provided an opportunity to discover for themselves the ramifications of gang
violence through structured exercises and interactive approaches to learning.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant/Co-op Agreement Amount:
extension: August 1, 2001 through January 15, 2002.

$192,432.00.

Funding period

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Executive
Director of the Sherifrs Community Based Programs be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

243595

RESOLUTION REGARDING THE REGULATION OF SIGNS APPROVED AND
ADOPTED JAN UA RY 20, 1999 (PROPOSED RESOLUTION AMENDMENT).
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by Herbert T. Schumann, Jr., County
Commissioner.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

AMENDING THE RESOLUTION REGARDING THE REGULATION OF SIGNS
APPROVED AND ADOPTED JANUARY 20, 1999
Whereas, the regulation and zoning control of signs in the unincorporated areas of Cook County
were adopted~ almost twenty-five years ago; and
Whereas, numerous conflicts have developed over the years between the growth and development
of the unincorpo rated areas and areas under municipal authority, and the proliferation of signs,
particularly large advertising signs; and
Whereas, signs permitted under the 1976 Cook County Zoning Ordinance are now considered out
of place, particularly in areas attempting to preserve scenic and aesthetic assets; and
Whereas, a comprehensive amendment to Article 12 of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance has
been proposed and introduced for consideration by the Cook County Board of Commissioners; and
Whereas, the proposed amendments have been referred to the Comm ittee on Zoning fo r public
hearing and comment, which process -ts was expected to take several months to complete; and
Whereas, these proposed sig n regulations have yet to be considered by the Committee on Zoning
and Building; and
Whereas, the proposed sign regulations wi ll substantially amend the size and location perm itted
fo r many signs, and will make certain sig ns non-confo rming subject to amortization and removal; and
\Vhereas, the ongoing iss1:1ance of b1:1i lding pem1its and/or zoning relief 1:111der the e><isting zoning
ordinanee 1:1nElerrn ines the ability of Cook Co1:1nty to effeeti,,el;' reg1:1late the proliferation of eonflieting
signs thro1:1gho1:1t the w1incorporateEI areas of Cook Co1:1nty.
Whereas the moratorium o n the issuance of permits for advertising s igns has been effective in
limiting the proliferation of advertising s igns, however, businesses in unincorporated Cook County are
seeking zoning re lief for the replacement and modernization of on premises advertising signs;
NOW THEREFORE, BE IT RESOL YEO AS FOLLOWS:
From the date of adoption of this Resolution and until review of the comprehensive
I.
amendment to Article 12 of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance has been completed, there shall be a
moratorium o n the issuance of any and all permits for the constructi on, expansion or relocation of all
signs or for zoning relief as regulated by Article 12 of the 1976 Cook County Zoning Ordinance.

1972

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 200 I
2.
The Commissioner of Building and Zoning shall, upon sufficient evidence submitted by
an applicant, have the authority to issue a permit for replacement of sign(s) located on and within the
premises of a business or property owner where such s ign(s) existed prior to the moratorium and which
have come into disrepair due to damage by weather conditions, accident, intentional acts of vandalism, et'
in instances where the business at which the existing sign is located has changed, or in instances in which
the property or business owner deems that an existing on premises sign no longer appropriately projects
the quality of the business and where. due to the age and deterioration of construction materials used,
such sign(s) detract from the value of the bus iness property. The issuance of a permit for the replacement
of previously existing s igns shall be only for restricted to applications for those on premises signs Hat
req1:1iring a variation from , and that meet the requirements of, the 1976 Cook County Zoning Ordinance.
The Commissioner of Building and Zoning shall take appropriate steps to inform the
3.
Zoning Administrator and the Zoning Board of Appeals of this relief under the moratorium.
lf, upon the expiration of six months from the date of adoption of this amended
4.
moratorium, review of the proposed amendments to Article 12 has not been concluded, 1fle this amended
moratorium hereby imposed shall be reviewed and the County Board shall determine whether a basis
exists to extend the moratorium for a further period of time.

Commissioner Schumann, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved to consider a substitute
amendment. The motion carried.
Commissioner Schumann, seconded by Commissioner Hansen moved to amend .2, Line 7 from
quality to identity. The motion carried.
Commissioner Schumann, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved the approval of
Communication No. 243595 as amended. The motion carried.
01-R-449
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE HERBERT T. SCHUMANN, JR., COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Amending the Resolution Regarding the Regulations of Signs
Approved and Adopted January 20, 1999
Whereas, the regulation and zoning control of sig ns in the unincorporated areas of Cook County
were adopted evei: almost twenty-five years ago; and
Whereas, numerous conflicts have developed over the years between the growth and development
of the unincorporated areas and areas under municipal authority, and the proliferation of signs, pmticularly
large advertising signs; and
Whereas, signs permitted under the 1976 Cook County Zoning Ordinance are now considered out
of place, particularly in areas attempting to preserve scenic and aesthetic assets; and
Whereas, a comprehensive amendment to Article 12 of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance has
been proposed and introduced for consideration by the Cook County Board of Commissioners; and

1973

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
Whereas, the proposed amendments have been referred to the Committee on Zoning for public
hearing and comment, which process is was expected to take several months to complete; and
Whereas, these proposed sign regulations have yet to be considered by the Committee on Zoning
and Building; and
Whereas, the proposed sign regulations will substantially amend the size and location permitted for
many signs, and will make certain signs non-conforming subject to amortization and removal; and
Wl"lereas, the ongoing iss1:1anee of l:milding permits and/or zoning relief 1:1nder the e"isting zoning
ordinanee 1:1ndermines the ability of Cook Co1:1nty to effeetiYely reg1:1late the proliferation of eonflieting signs
thro1:1gho1:1tthe tmineorporated areas of Cook Co1:1nty.
Whereas the moratorium on the issuance of permits for advertising signs has been effective in
limiting the proliferation of advertising signs, however, businesses in unincorporated Cook County are
seeking zoning relief for the replacement and modernization of on premises advertising signs;
NOW THEREFORE, BE IT RESOL YEO AS FOLLOWS:
From the date of adoption of this Resolution and until review of the comprehensive
I.
amendment to Article 12 of the Cook County Zoning Ordinance has been completed, there shall be a
moratorium on the issuance of any and all permits for the construction, expansion or relocation of all signs
or for zoning relief as regulated by Article 12 of the 1976 Cook County Zoning Ordinance, excepting as
enumerated in paragraph 2 below.
The Commissioner of Building and Zoning shall, upon sufficient evidence submitted by
2.
an applicant, have the authority to issue a permit for replacement of sign(s) located on and within the
premises of a business or property owner where such sign(s) existed prior to the moratorium and which
have come into disrepair due to damage by weather conditions, accident, intentional acts of vandalism, or
in instances where the business at which the existing sign is located has changed,. Additionally, the
Commissioner of Building and Zoning shall have authority to issue a permit for the replacement of an on
premises sign~ in instances in which the property or business owner deems that an existing on premises
sign no longer appropriately projects the qulllity identity of the business and where, due to the age and/or
deterioration of construction materials used, such sign(s) detract from the value of the business property.
The issuance of a permit for the replacement of previously existing signs shall be only for restricted to
applications for those on premises signs not req1:1iring a variation from, and that meet conform to or
require a variance from the req1:1irements provisions of, ARTICLE 12 of the 1976 Cook County Zoning
Ordinance.
3.
The Commissioner of Building and Zoning shall take appropriate steps to inform the
Zoning Admini strator and the Zoning Board of Appeals of this relief under the moratorium.
4.
If, upon the expiration of six months from the date of adoption of this amended
moratorium, review of the proposed amendments to Article 12 has not been concluded, the this amended
moratorium hereby imposed shall be reviewed and the County Board shall determine whether a basis exists
to extend the moratorium for a further period of time.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of June 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Comm it1ee on Finance of the Board of Commi ssioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice on
Tuesday, May I, 200 1, at the hour of 2:00 P.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building, 118
North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois, for the purpose of conducting a public hearing regarding the
proposed Cook County Longtime Homeowner Property Tax Assessment Exemption Ordinance.

1975

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
242044

COOK COUNTY LONGTIME HOMEOWNER PROPERTY TAX ASSESSMENT
EXEMPTION ORDINANCE (PROPOSED ORDINANCE).
Submitting a Proposed
Ordinance sponsored by Roberto Maldonado, County Commissioner; Co-Sponsored by
Bobbie L. Steele, Earlean Collins, Carl R. Hansen, William R. Moran, Joseph Mario Moreno,
Deborah Sims, Mike Quigley and Calvin R. Sutker, County Commissioners.
The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

COOK COUNTY LONGTIME HOMEOWNER PROPERTY
TAX ASSESSMENT EXEMPTION ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, longtime homeowners are experiencing substantial and unpredictable property
tax increases due to upper-scale development or redevelopment, known as gentrification, in
their communities; and
WHEREAS, in recognition of the severe economic circumstances many of these longtime
homeowners have faced, the Illinois Legislature passed Public Act 88-451 , the Longtime
Owner-Occupant Property Tax Relief Act (35 ILCS 250, et. seq.), in August, 1993; and
WHEREAS, on July 24, 1998, the Illinois Legislature passed Public Act 90-0648, amending
the Longtime Owner-Occupant Property Tax Relief Act to require the participation of the
City of Chicago and the Board of Education, which are the two largest taxing bodies in Cook
County; and
WHEREAS, the purpose of the Act is to provide property tax relief to longtime
homeowners, whose property taxes have risen sharply as a result of new construction or
renovation of existing residences in long-established residential areas; and
WHEREAS, counties, having a population of 100,000 or more, are authorized to enact an
ordinance, in accordance with the provisions of the Act, that provides for property tax relief;
and
WHEREAS, purs uant to the Act, as a county with a population of more than I 00,000, Cook
County is authori zed to enact an ordinance to provide tax relief to longtime homeowners
within the County that may be eligible under the provisions set forth in the Act; and
WHEREAS, as a matter of public policy, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has the
authority and the responsibility to enact property tax relief provi sions that will enable eligible
longtime homeowners to remain in financially secure possession of their homes.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the President and the Board of
Commissioners of Cook County the following:
TITLE OF ORDINANCE: (New) Cook County Longtime Homeowner Property Tax
Assessment Exemption Ordinance.

1976

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR J UNE 5, 2001
An Ordinance creating the Longtime Homeowner Exemption Program to provide property
tax relief to homeowners who have owned and occupied their homes for ten years or more.
The Cook County Assessor ("Assessor") shall administer the Longtime Homeowner
Program. To be eligible, the longtime homeowner must own and reside in a Class 2 property
located in Cook County. The property must have an assessment increase that exceeds one
and one-half (I I /2) times the percentage median assessment increase for Class 2 properties
within the assessment di strict where the property is located. That portion of an eligible
homeowner's assessment, which exceeds one and one-half (I 1/2) times the percentage
median assessment increase within the assessment district, shall be exempted in the
calculation of the property tax. Eligibility for the program terminates at the time the
homeowner no longer occupies the property as a principal residence, the title to the property
is transferred, or the Assessor determines that the homeowner' s assessment increase no
longer exceeds one and one-half (I 1/2) times the percentage median assessment increase
within the assessment district.

County Longtime Homeowner Exemption Ordinance" has been subm itted by Commissioner Maldonado.

Chairman Daley entered responses to his questions from Assessor Houlihan and Clerk Orr, along with
supplementary letters from the offices of the Assessor, County Clerk and Treasurer into the record. (The
referenced documents are on file in the Office of the County Clerk.)

Following testimony, Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved to
accept the substitute version for the proposed ordinance in Item 242044. The motion carried.
Commissioner Moran voted present.
In response to Commissioner Lechowicz's question regarding how the cap of $300,000 was determined,
Veronica Lynch, Chief Deputy Assessor, responded there were several numbers that the sponsor of the
ordinance talked about in terms of the cap level as well as a group comprised of staff from the offices of
the County Clerk, Assessor, President and Commissioner Maldonado. Ms. Lynch stated Commissioner
Maldonado chose $300,000 as the cap on the market value of a home.
In response to Commissioner Silvestri's question regarding the $300,000 cap referred to as the assessed
value not the market value, Ms. Lynch responded the $300,000 refers to the Assessor's market value, and
not the assessed value.
In correspondence received from the Treasurer's Office, James Crawley suggested that a deadline should
be set for the filing for this exemption so that homeowners cannot apply for a certificate of error, as they
can do now for the homeowner's exemption and senior citizen' s exemption. The Treasurer's office
processes between fifty thousand and seventy thousand refunds annually, most of which are because
people fai l to apply for their homeowner's exemption. If property owners are allowed to go back in time
and apply for this longtime homeowner's exemption by way of a certificate of error, the number of
refunds to be processed would increase to approximately one hundred thousand per year.
Chairman Daley asked Cathy Maras O'Leary, Chief Information Officer, Bureau of Information
Technology and Automation, to respond to comments made by Mr. Crawley, regarding the processing of
the longtime homeowner exemption.
Mrs. O'Leary stated that these exemptions would be treated like a certificate of error. The certificates of
error are currently automated, and a different reason code will be added to reflect longtime homeowners.
Mrs. O'Leary stated the system can be modified very quickly to automate this type of refund.
Chairman Daley asked Mrs. O ' Leary to confirm that there will be no problem going back ifa person files
for this exemption?
Mrs. O' Leary replied no, certificates of error are already automated . A different reason code will just be
added. She stated her office has been working with the Assessor's office on this issue, and if anyone does
mi ss applying for this exemption and they need a refund, a different type of certificate of error (C of E)
will be created.

1983

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
Commissioner Maldonado stated the Treasurer's Office provided him with the percentage of homeowners
that failed to apply in time for the traditional homeowner's exemption, as approximately one percent.
Based on the estimates provided by the Assessor's Office that forty-two thousand homeowners may be
eligible for this exemption, and if one percent fail to apply, that translates to 420 homeowners that may
apply for a certificate of error. Would that really create a major burden in the Treasurer's office to
process 420 additional certificates of error?
Mr. Crawley responded that there are 1.6 million tax parcels in Cook County and currently the
Treasurer's Office processes between fifty thousand and seventy thousand certificate of error refunds.
With respect to the forty-two thousand homeowners in the Chicago assessment district that will be
eligible for this exemption, it can be assumed that a large portion of the people will not apply on a timely
basis because it is a new exemption and people may simply not know of its existence.
Chairman Daley stated in his opinion most people are going to assume that they will qualify for the
longtime homeowner exemption. Unfortunately, they will not.
In response to Commissioner Steele's question regarding the eligibility criteria, Veronica Lynch
responded there are essentially two qualifications. The qualifications are: the property is under the
$300,000 market value, and you have to have lived there ten years or more. Based on these
qualifications, the Assessor' s Office estimated between forty-two thousand and forty-nine thousand as the
number of eligible homeowners.
Chairman Daley asked Ms. Lynch how the number of eligible homeowners was determined?
Ms. Lynch responded the Assessor's Office looked back at residential sales in the last ten years, and at the
market value of that home. Based on this analysis, the universe of forty-two thousand and forty-nine
thousand was arrived at.
In response to Commissioner Steele's question regarding the qualification for the homestead exemption,
Ms. Lynch stated you have to have lived in your home from January first.
Chairman Daley asked Ms. Lynch what the assessed valuation would be on a $300,000 market value
home?
Ms. Lynch responded the assessed value would be $48,000.
Commissioner Lechowicz referenced a letter from Treasurer Pappas dated May 21, 200 I and attached to
that letter is correspondence dated March 7, 200 I from the Chief Information Officer, Cathy Maras
O'Leary to Patricia Shymanski, Acting Chief of Staff to the President. In the letter, Mrs. O ' Leary stated
two crucial points that cannot be overlooked: before the Department for Management of Information
Systems (MIS) can even begin modifying the required programs, detailed requirements are needed to be
completed by the affected agencies. Modifying approximately five hundred programs will take ten to
twelve months for five MIS programmers to complete. During that time no other requests can be worked
on for the Treasurer, County Clerk, Assessor, Board of Review or any other agency. Commissioner
Lechowicz asked Mrs. O' Leary to respond.
Mrs. O ' Leary responded that if this ordinance is passed, this would be a prioritized task that MIS would
do. What that means is that other requested modifications to coding might not be able to be done because
this is a priority for the Board. If this is the highest priority, we will have to focus most of our attention
on these priority items. She continued by stating there are five hundred programs that are not due to be
completed until next year. For the second installment tax bill, MIS does not have to change five hundred
programs. She believes MIS has six weeks of programming to be completed to accommodate this
ordinance.

1984

 JOURNA L OF PROCEEDI NGS FOR JUNE 5, 200 1
Chairman Daley called upon representati ves fro m the Assessor, County Clerk, and MIS, who have been
working together on this ordinance, its impact on their respective offices, and its implementation.
Fredda Bennan, Director of Real Estate & Tax Services, County Clerk's office, explained the differential
in the calculations. The calculations referenced in her letter refer to how the exemption wi ll affect a
property owner who app lies for the exemption. Assuming the exemption is passed, and the e ligible
homeowner applies, she has determined how much they would save because they have applied for this
exemption. The figure is attributable to the amount of equalized assessed value that is removed from the

municipality and the school district can opt out. Mr. Vaselopulos stated if a taxing district, for example a
school district, chooses to opt out, they would not participate in providing a break to the taxpayers that are
eligible within their district. The school district would not allow that the equalized assessed valuation be
reduced for those properties. Consequently, the tax rates for those districts that chose to opt out would
remain low. The other districts which don' t have a choice and could not opt out, and any reduction that
occurred due to the exemption, their equalized assessed valuation would be reduced and the rates would
go up a little for those other taxing districts that cannot opt out.

Commissioner Silvestri asked ASA Prinzi to provide him with the legislative history on this statute.
ASA Prinzi stated the statute originally passed in 1993, and has undergone a series of amendments. The
statute relating to the non-opt-out provisions for the City of Chicago and the Chicago Board of Education
passed in 1998. As a matter of general principal statewide, the sponsors of the statute wanted to have local
taxing districts, particularly municipalities and school boards, to be able to control their expenditures. One
factor of the expenditure is the cost of the exemption. In the case of the City of Chicago, the sponsors
wanted to have the two largest taxing bodies within that ambit to be involved. If the City of Chicago and the
Chicago Board of Education could opt out there would be no effect to the statute.

The Committee commenced consideration of the amendments:

AMENDMENT #1
Sponsor:

Commissioner Mike Quigley

Co-Sponsor:

Commissioner Earlean Collins

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
THE SURVIVING SPOUSE AMENDMENT, amends the Cook County Longtime Homeowner
Exemption Ordinance. This amendment will allow an inheriting spouse to potentially qualify for the
H.E.L.P. exemption when his/her spouse passes away, even if the surviving spouse was never listed as an
owner of the property. With this amendment, when a spouse listed as an owner of record passes away
and leaves the property to the surviving spouse, the surviving spouse may "tack on" the deceased spouse's
ownership time in order to qualify for the exemption, provided the remaining criteria are also met.

Amends:

Section 3 - Definitions.

SECTION 3. DEFINITIONS. As used in this Ordinance:
"Assessment District." Cook County has a triennial reassessment cycle wherein one of the three di stricts
within the county is reassessed each year. The three assessment districts are defined in the Illinois
Property Tax Code (35 ILCS 200/9-220(8)).

"AV."

Assessed Value as defined in the Cook County Real Property Assessment Classification
Ordinance (Section 2, Class 2 and Section 3, Class 2).

1991

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 200 I
"Average Assessment .Increase." A percentage calculated by taking the value of all potentially
qualifying Class 2 properties within the assessment district and determining the percent difference
between the current reassessment value and the prior year's assessment value.
"EAV." Equalized Assessed Value. The assessed value multiplied by the equalization factor calculated
by the Illinois Department of Revenue.
"H.E.L.P." Homeowner Exemption for Long-term Properties calculated as follows: that portion of
the current EA V for an eligible property which exceeds the sum of: (1) the EA V for the year prior to
reassessment; plus (2) the prior year EAV multiplied by a factor equal to 150% of the average assessment
increase for the most current reassessment of the assessment district.
"Class 2 Properties." Residential properties as defined in the Cook County Real Property Assessment
Classification Ordinance (Section 2, Class 2).
"Longtime Homeowners." Persons who have owned and occupied a Cook County Class 2 property for
ten years or more as their principal residence, or five years or more ifthe owner received assistance in the
acquisition of the property as part of a government or non-profit housing program. "Longtime
homeowners" also means persons who inherited the property from a spouse who owned and occupied a
Class 2 property for ten years or more as their principal residence or five years or more if the owner
received assistance in purchasing the residence from a governmental or non-profit housing program.
"Triennial Reassessment." Any reassessment of an assessment district, which occurs every third year as
set forth in the Illinois Property Tax Code (35 JLCS 200/9-220(8)).
Leave was granted to add Commissioner Collins as a co-sponsor.
Chairman Daley recognized Commissioner Quigley to provide a summary of the amendment.
Comm issioner Quigley stated this amendment, otherwise known as the surviving spouse amendment,
takes into consideration a surviving spouse who was never listed as the owner of the property. The
widow or widower would not fall under the protection of this ordinance without the passage of this
amendment. The amendment basically allows this person to be listed as the owner of record. If the
owner of record passes away and leaves the property to the surviving spouse, the surviving spouse may
tack on the deceased spouse's ownership time in order to qualify for the exemption, which has a ten-year
requirement.
Commissioner Lechowicz expressed support for this amendment, however he asked if there would be a
problem in the administration of this amendment. Currently the Recorder of Deeds office maintains the
records with respect to the title for the property. The Treasurer's office is provided information as it
relates to the tax bill itself. Commissioner Lechowicz asked if any of the offices involved would have
any problem administering the provisions contained in this amendment.
Jim Crawley, representing the Treasurer' s Office, responded that the Treasurer' s office would not be the
office responsible for providing the information to the Assessor. Mr. Crawley explained that the forms
are sent from the Recorder of Deeds office to the Assessor's office, then to the Illinois Department of
Revenue.
Ms. Lynch responded that the Assessor's office would not have any problem administering the provisions
of this amendment.

1992

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
Commissioner Silvestri concurs with the amendment, but asked if there is a requirement that the couple
be married for a certain period of time.
Commissioner Quigley responded that the amendment only requires that they be married. He believes
that was the legislative intent.
Commissioner Quigley, seconded by Commissioner Lechowicz, moved approval of Amendment #1.
The motion carried unanimously.
Chairman Daley proceeded with Amendment #2.
AMENDMENT #2
Sponsor:

Commissioner Mike Quigley

Co-Sponsor:

Commissioner Earlean Collins

Explanation (purpose) of Amendment:
This amendment incorporates a means test into the Proposed Ordinance. The legislative history of the
enabling statute indicates that the statute was designed to provide property tax relief for longtime low and
middle-income residents of Cook County. This means test amendment will allow the Ordinance to
comport with legislative intent and provide relief for those longtime residents who need it most. The
amendment will limit eligibility to those whose household income does not exceed 115% of the Chicago
Primary Metropolitan Statistical Area median income as defined by the United States Department of
Housing and Urban Development. For FY 2001, this would limit eligibility for a one-person household
to an annual income of $56,000 or less. A four-person household would qualify with an annual
household income of $81 ,075 or less.
Amends:

Section 5 - Eligibility Criteria

SECTION 5. ELIGIBILITY CRITERIA.
The following nonexclusive criteria shall be used to verify a longtime homeowner's eligibility for the
H.E.L.P. program on an annual basis:
( 1)

Homeowner is an owner-occupant of a Cook County Class 2 property, and that property has
been the homeowner's principal residence for at least ten consecutive years as of January I
of the reassessment year. A homeowner may become eligible for an exemption in a year
subsequent to the reassessment if a ten year consecutive residency has been established by
January 1 of that year; or

(2)

Homeowner is an owner-occupant of a Cook County Class 2 property, and that property has
been the homeowner's principal residence for at least five consecutive years if the
homeowner received assistance in the acquisition of the property as part of a government or
nonprofit housing program under the following guidelines:
(a)

The program is restricted to qualified homebuyers on the basis of the household
income of the homebuyer; and

1993

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
(b)

The income restriction for the home buyer did not exceed 120% of the area median
income as defined by the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development; and

(c)

The subsidy exceeds $5,000 or 5% of the development cost of the property, whichever
is greater; and

(d)

The homebuyer is restricted from selling the house at full market price for at least five
years from the date of purchase.

The Cook County Board shall determine whether a purchase assistance program is qualified
under the provisions of this Ordinance; and
(3)

Homeowner' s property must have an AV increase that exceeds 150% of the current average
AV increase for Class 2 properties in the assessment district where the property is located;
and

(4)

HomeowAer' s property earmot ha't'e a market vah,1e used for assessmeAt purposes that
e>rneeds $300,000 iA the eurrent reassessment )'ear Homeowner's annual household income
for the year of the homeowner's triennial assessment does not exceed one hundred and
fifteen percent ( 115%) of the Chicago Primary Metropolitan Statistical Area median income
as defined by the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development; and

(5)

For any triennial assessment cycle, homeowner did not cause a substantial improvement
which resulted in an increase in fair cash value in the property in excess of the $45,000
allowance as set forth in the Illinois Property Tax Code (35 ILCS 200/15-180).

Leave was granted to add Commissioner Collins as a co-sponsor.
Chairman Daley recognized Commissioner Quigley to provide a summary of the amendment.
Commissioner Quigley stated this ordinance is an attempt to deal with an inequity in a system that is
basically inequitable when considering one's ability to pay. Commissioner Quigley referenced criteria in
the statute such as, the County may impose such qualifying criteria as age and income. However, the
statute does not address how expensive the property is, in terms of putting limitations on participation in
the program. It addresses factors such as the ten-year requirement, the property is owner-occupied, and
how big the building is. The statute is targeting lower and middle class people who, through no fault of
their own, are put in a position where they can' t afford to live in their own neighborhoods. They are
forced to sell their property at an expense. While they enjoy that capital gain, through our taxing policies
we have further changed the scope and the nature of that neighborhood and exacerbated an inequitable
program. Therefore, it makes sense to make income one of the qualifying criteria. The statute references
areas that are rapidly experiencing gentrification, however including a cap of $300,000 would decrease
the number of those eligible even though their assessments have increased so much. A means test is used
with other property tax programs, such as CHAPS.
Commissioner Quigley continued by stating that this amendment creates a means test. The numbers used
are the 2001 HUD income guidelines based on the Chicago Primary Metropolitan Statistical Area. The
figures were derived from these tables based on the household size and family income. Therefore it
would not be necessary to pass legislation every year depending on what the cost of living is.
Commissioner Quigley encourages passage of this amendment as a reasonable way to accomplish and
fulfill the spirit and purpose of this statute as it applies to the people of Cook County.

1994

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001

means test associated with that. The Department of Revenue is required to audit the information provided
to our office in order to ensure the accuracy of the income data.
Ms. Ly nch stated there are administrative issues with a means test that is placed on the Assessor's Office,

program based on a means test. The Assessor' s office would only be able to verify the assessed value of
the home and how long someone lived in a home . Whether or not anyone lived in a home at a certain
income cap becomes more difficult for the Assessor to verify.
Chairman Daley called upon Cathy Maras O' Leary, Chief Information Officer, Bureau of Information

no burden on the Department for Management oflnformation Systems (MIS) at all.
Chairman Daley asked Mrs. O' Leary, for clarification purposes, would MIS have a burden implementing
this?
Mrs. O' Leary responded that MIS would not have any burden, the burden administratively is on the
Assessor.

Ms. Berman responded that the burden is on the Assessor's Office, not the County Clerk' s Office. The
County C lerk's office would process those people identified by the Assessor as being eligible.
C hairman Daley called upon Assistant State's Attorney, Michael Prinzi.

items one throug h two ( d) of Amendment #2.

1995

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 200 I
ASA Prinzi commented that the language in the substitute ordinance or in Amendment #2 could be

chooses to use it. The Board could even eliminate this criteria if you did not want to use it. ASA Prinzi
stated that Commissioner Quigley suggests a specific way to determine an income value, and then base
eligibility on that. Whereas, Commissioner Maldonado suggests a cutoff based on property value, in
which you infer a person's ability to pay. Either criteria involves the ability to pay. Therefore, from a
legal perspective either proposal would stand.
Commissioner Lechowicz asked for an explanation of section 5 (2) (b), wherein the homebuyer is

amendment.
Commissioner Lechowicz believes it will be difficult initially to get the ordinance in operation and
perform the necessary administrative functions in order to determine the eligible homes. He recognizes
the time and effort that was spent by Commissioner Maldonado, Commissioner Daley and the
administration on this proposed ordinance. Commissioner Lechowicz commented that this means test
could be construed as a litmus test on this ordinance and potentially jeopardizes the ordinance itself.
Commissioner Schumann commented that there is a lot of speculation with this ordinance on what the
intent of the Legislature was, who is going to be affected, how the suburbs fare versus the City. This
amendment applies to those individuals on a fixed or low income in the suburbs and the City of Chicago,
and makes them eligible for the exemption.
Commissioner Steele commended Commissioner Maldonado for his vision and leadership. However, this
ordinance may not really reach the people that it is intended to reach. Commissioner Steele expressed her
support for the use of the income criteria versus the property value.
Comm issioner Goslin expressed his support of this amendment. He noted that both he and Commissioner
Quigley have remarkably similar districts demographically speaking. In his district, the rise in property

amendment adds to the "challengeability" of the ord inance?
ASA Prinzi does not believe that Amendment #2 adds to the " challengeability" of the ordinance. He
stated this is a lesser problem .
Commissioner Sutker stated he appreciates all of the work that has gone into this ordinance and all of the

alluded to by various speakers. However, because there is so much uncertainty, and there may well be
litigation with respect to this ordinance, certainly as it concerns the school board and municipalities of
this County, it is important to include a means test. Commissioner Sutker stated that real estate taxes are

1996

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
a regressive tax. The ability to pay is a critical factor. Those who are able to pay should be paying the
full amount of the real estate tax that their property requires. This amendment adds credibility to the
entire ordinance. Commissioner Sutker concluded by stating this ordinance will need to be readdressed
when the next assessment infonnation is made available in November.

Chairman Daley recognized Veronica Lynch, Chief Deputy Assessor.
Ms. Lynch clarified that in its first year of implementation as it relates to the City of Chicago, the

data provided for the senior freeze. The Department of Revenue has an audit function with res pect to the

Chairman Daley stated he will be supporting this amendment because the means test is a good tool to

numbers provided, forty percent may save fifteen dollars, and seventy-five percent may save one
thousand five hundred. By the time you get to that level the house is already too expensive for you to live
in if you are on a fi xed income and that is not going to change.

Ms. Ly nch responded in the affirmative.

Ms. Lynch responded that it does affect the assessed value of the home, but there is a four to six year
period before that assessment increase would kick in, based on the time you were issued the permit.

Ms. Lynch responded that there is a greater degree of control with this provision.
In response to Commissioner Collins' s question regarding the need for the new construction provision,
ASA Prinzi stated that section five is a disqualifier. ASA Prinzi stated the $45,000 allowance is
referenced in the property tax code. For purposes of this ordinance, it just delineates that number and it
refers back to the statute, if you can make substantial improvements to your property you can probably
afford to pay the taxes. If someone makes a $30,000 improvement to their home, that assessed value
(AV), or that market value translated to AV is not added to the value for tax purposes.
Chairman Daley thanked all of the members and Commissioner Maldonado for their hard work and

however, it is the only thing we have been given by the General Assembly. He continued by stating he
believes many people will misunderstand the term "longtime homeowner," and they are not going to
benefit; however it is a beginning.

01-0-12
ORDINANCE

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ROBERTO MALDONADO, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE BOBBIE L. STEELE, EARLEAN COLLINS, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, TED LECHOWICZ, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, DEBORAH SIMS,
MIKE QUIGLEY AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
LONGTIME HOMEOWNER EXEMPTION ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, longtime homeowners are experiencing substantial and unpredictable property tax
increases due to upper-scale development or redevelopment, known as gentrification, in their
communities; and
WHEREAS, in recog111t1on of the severe economic circumstances many of these longtime
homeowners have faced, the Illinois Legislature passed Public Act 88-451 , the Longtime OwnerOccupant Property Tax Relief Act (35 lLCS 250, et. seq.), in August, 1993; and
WHEREAS, on July 24, 1998, the Illinois Legislature passed Public Act 90-0648, amending the
Longtime Owner-Occupant Property Tax Relief Act to require the participation of the City of Chicago
and the Board of Education, which are the two largest taxing bodies in Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the purpose of the Act is to provide property tax relief to longtime homeowners,
whose property taxes have risen s harply as a result of new construction or renovation of existing
residences in long-established residential areas; and
WHEREAS, counties, having a population of l 00,000 or more, are authorized to enact an
ordinance, in accordance with the provisions of the Act, that provides for property tax relief; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to the Act, as a county with a population of more than 100,000, Cook
County is authorized to enact an ordinance to provide tax relief to longtime homeowners within the
County that may be eligible under the provisions set forth in the Act; and

1999

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
WHEREAS, as a matter of public policy, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has the
authority and the responsibility to enact property tax relief provisions that will enable eligible longtime
homeowners to remain in financially secure possession of their homes.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the President and the Board of Commissioners
of Cook County the following:
TITLE OF ORDINANCE: (New) Longtime Homeowner Exemption Ordinance.
An Ordinance creating the Homeowner Exemption for Long-term Properties ("H.E.L.P.") Program to
provide property tax relief to certain longtime homeowners in established neighborhoods who are facing a
dramatic rise in property taxes directly or indirectly attributable to gentrification. To be eligible, the
longtime homeowner must own and reside in a Cook County Class 2 property for a minimum of ten
years, or five years if the homeowner received assistance in the acquisition of the property as part of a
government or nonprofit housing program . The homeowner will be ineligible ifthe property has a market
value for assessment purposes exceeding $300,000 in the current reassessment year or substantial
improvement which resulted in an increase in fair cash value in excess of the $45,000 allowance as set
forth in the Illinois Property Tax Code. The Assessor shall verify potential eligible homeowners on an
annual basis and provide to the Cook County Clerk the information necessary to calculate the exemption
in accordance with the provisions set forth in this Ordinance. The Cook County Clerk shall then remove
the exempt value from the calculation of the property tax and the Cook County Treasurer shall state on
the tax bill the amount of tax saved by the exemption.
SECTION 1. SHORT TITLE. This Ordinance shall be known and may be cited as the "Longtime
Homeowner Exemption Ordinance."
SECTION 2. PURPOSE. The intent of this Ordinance is to stabilize the effects of soaring property
taxes for longtime homeowners who otherwise may be displaced from neighborhoods where
gentrification is occurring.
SECTION 3. DEFINITIONS. As used in this Ordinance:
"Assessment District." Cook County has a triennial reassessment cycle wherein one of the three di stricts
within the county is reassessed each year. The three assessment districts are defined in the Illinois
Property Tax Code (35 ILCS 200/9-220(B)).
"AV." Assessed Value as defined in the Cook County Real Property Assessment Classification
Ordinance (Section 2, Class 2 and Section 3, Class 2).
"Average Assessment Increase." A percentage calculated by taking the value of all potentially
qualifying Class 2 properties within the assessment district and determining the percent difference
between the current reassessment value and the prior year's assessment value.
"EAV." Equalized Assessed Value. The assessed value multiplied by the equalization factor calculated
by the Illinois Department of Revenue.
"H.E.L.P." Homeowner Exemption for Long-term Properties calculated as follows: that portion of
the current EA V for an eligible property which exceeds the sum of: (I) the EA V for the year prior to
reassessment; plus (2) the prior year EA V multiplied by a factor equal to 150% of the average assessment
increase for the most current reassessment of the assessment district.

2000

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR J UNE 5, 2001

"Class 2 Properties." Residential properties as defined in the Cook County Real Property Assessment
Classification Ordinance (Section 2, C lass 2).

"Longtime Homeowners." Persons who have owned and occupied a Cook County Class 2 property for
ten years or more as their principal residence, or five years or more ifthe owner received assistance in the
acquisition of the property as part of a government or nonprofit housing program. " Longtime
homeowners" also means persons who in herited the property from a spouse who owned and occupied a
Class 2 property for ten years or more as their principal residence or five years or more if the owner
received ass istance in purchasing the residence from a governmental or non-profit housing program.

"Triennial Reassessment." Any reassessment of an assessment district, which occurs every third year as
set forth in the Illinois Property Tax Code (35 ILCS 200/9-220(8)).

SECTION 4. ADMINISTRATION OF THE HOMEOWNER EXEMPTION FOR LONG-TERM
PROPERTIES ("H.E.L.P.") PROGRAM.
(A)

The Cook County Assessor shall have the authority to:
( I)

Administer the Homeowner Exemption for Long-term Properties ("H.E.L.P. ") program as
created by the enactment of this Ordinance and;

(2)

Create applications for and determine potential eligibility to the program based on the
eligibility criteria set forth in this Ordinance and;

(B) The Cook County Clerk shal l have the authority to compute tax rates and calculate tax bill amounts
and to provide this information to the Cook County Treas urer to implement the provisions of this
Ordinance.

(C)

The Cook County Treas urer shall state on the tax bill the amount of the tax saved by the exemption.

SECTION 5. ELIGIBILITY CRITERIA.
T he following nonexclusive cri teria shall be used to verify a longtime homeowner's el igibility for the
H.E.L.P. program on an annual basis:
( 1)

Homeowner is an owner-occupant of a Cook County Class 2 property, and that property has
been the homeowner's principal residence for at least ten consecutive years as of January 1
of the reassessment year. A homeowner may become elig ible for an exemption in a year
subsequent to the reassessment if a ten year consecutive res idency has been established by
Jan uary I of that year; or

(2)

Homeowner is an owner-occupant of a Cook County C lass 2 property, and that property has
been the homeowner's principal residence for at least five consecutive years if the
homeowner received assistance in the acquisition of the property as part of a government or
nonprofit housing program under the fo llowing guidelines:
(a)

The program is restricted to qualified homebuyers on the basis of the household
income of the homebuyer; and

(b)

The income restriction for the home buyer did not exceed 120% of the area median
income as defined by the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development; and

200 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 2001
(c)

The subsidy exceeds $5,000 or 5% of the development cost of the property, whichever
is greater; and

(d)

The homebuyer is restricted from selling the house at full market price for at least five
years from the date of purchase.

The Cook County Board shall detennine whether a purchase assistance program is
qualified under the provisions of this Ordinance; and

(3)

Homeowner's property must have an AV increase that exceeds 150% of the current average
AV increase for C lass 2 properties in the assessment district where the property is located;
and

(4)

I lomeowAer's property eaAAOt ha'<'e a market 't alue used fo r assessmeAt purposes that
exeeeds $300,000 iA the eurreAt reassessmeAt year Homeowner's annual household income
for the year of the homeowner's trienni al assessment does not exceed one hundred and
fifteen percent (11 5%) of the Chicago Primary Metropolitan Statistical Area median income
as defined by the United States Department of Housing and Urban Development; and

(5)

For any triennial assessment cycle, homeowner did not cause a substantial improvement
which resulted in an increase in fair cash value in the property in excess of the $45,000
allowance as set fo rth in the Illinois Property Tax Code (35 ILCS 200/ 15-180).

1

SECTION 6. APPLYING THE EXEMPTION.
(A)

The Cook County Assessor shall:
( I)

Annually verify potentia l e ligible homeowners; and

(2)

Provide to the Cook County Clerk the information necessary to calculate the exemption in
accordance with the Ordinance.

(B)

The Cook County Clerk shall remove the exempt value from the calculation of the property tax.

(C)

The Cook County Treasurer shall state on the tax bill the amount of tax saved by the exemption.

SECTION 7. ELIGIBILITY NOTIFICATION.
The Assessor shall notify pote ntially eligible owners of record of Class 2 properties in Cook County of
the existence of the Longtime Homeowners Exemption Program fo r each trien nial assessment cycle
w ithin sufficient time to apply.

SECTION 8. APPLICATION.
This Ordinance shall first apply to the assessment district of the 2000 tax year and to each assessment
district thereafter.

SECTION 9. REQUIREMENTS FOR DETERMINATION OF PARTICIPATION.
Any taxing agency exercising the provision(s) in the Longtime Owner-Occupant Property Tax Relief Act
(35 ILCS 250, et. seq.) shall:

2002

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 200 I
( 1)

File a resolution or ordinance with the Cook County Clerk no later than the last Tuesday in
December of the year for which the taxes are assessed; and

(2)

In the event that any taxing agency adopts eligibility standards or criteria which differ from
those provided herein at Section 5, the taxing agency shall certify a list of parcels (Permanent
Index Numbers) deemed eligible by the taxing agency to the Cook County Assessor no later
than the last Tuesday in December of the year for which the taxes are assessed.

SECTION 10. EFFECTIVE DATE.
This Ordinance takes effect upon becoming law.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of June 2001.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

RESOLUTION

THE HONORABLE WILLIAM R. MORAN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,

PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND CALVIN R. SUTKER, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, in May of 1776 Betsy Ross completed the first American Flag; and
WHEREAS, the Flag designed by Betsy Ross was adopted as the flag of the United States of America on
June 14, 1777 by the first Flag Act; and

2072

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUN E 5, 2001

WHEREAS, the Flag Act of 1777 resolved that the Uni ted States of America's flag would be 13
alternating red and white stripes with a blue union containing thirteen white stars representing a new
constellation; and
WHEREAS, the Flag Act of 1794 added two stripes and two stars after May of 1795 in order to
recognize the statehood of Kentucky and Vermont; and
WHEREAS, in 1818 the Flag of the United States was set at thirteen stripes and twenty stars, one for
each state, with stars added for new states on July 4th of the year after their admission; and
WHEREAS, the pattern for the stars was set in 19 12 by an Executive Order from President Taft, after
New Mexico and Arizona were granted statehood, with six horizontal rows of eight stars with a single
point of each star pointing upward ; and
WHEREAS, the most recent star was added in 1960 for the State of Hawaii, and the Flag was given it 's
current design by Executive Order of President Eisenhower, nine rows of stars staggered horizontally and
eleven rows staggered vertically; and
WHEREAS, after BJ Cigrand, a Wisconsin schoolteacher celebrated June 14, 1885 as Flag Birthday with
his students, numerous magazines and newspapers adopted the term and advocated for the observance of
Flag Day; and
WHEREAS, several states and cities began to recognize Flag Day as June 14th, Chicago he ld a Flag Day
celebration with over 300,000 school chi ldren in 1894 in parks across the city; and
WHEREAS, Flag Day was officially established on August 3, 1949 by a Joint Resolution of Congress
signed by President Truman; and
WHEREAS, Flag Week was established for the week in which June 14th falls, by a Joint Resolution of
Congress signed by President Johnson on June 9, 1966; and
WHEREAS, each June the President of the United States issues a proclamation in accordance with the
resolutions approved by Congress in 1949 and 1966 designating June 14th as Flag Day and the week in
which June 14th fa lls as Flag Week; and
WHEREAS, the Flag of the United States of America has flown proudly, in all it ' s forms across the
nation since 1776 and around the world since 1787, from the heights of Pike's Peak since 1820, Mount
Everest since 1963 and the Moon since Ju ly 20, 1969.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and the Cook County Board of
Commissioners does hereby recognize June 14, 2001 as Flag Day and the week beginning June 10, 200 I
as Flag Week and ask that during th is week the citizens of Cook County proudly display the Flag of the
United States of America and honor the Flag that has a history as rich as the history of our Nation itself.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of June 200 I.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA VlD ORR, County C lerk

2073

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 200 I

Commissioner Moran, seconded by Comm issioner Carr, moved that the Resol ution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

HONORING SOL J. ROCKE ON HIS RETIREMENT AS
VILLAGE PRESIDENT OF THE VILLAGE OF HAZEL CREST
WHEREAS, Doctor Sol J. Rocke has been the Village President of Hazel Crest fo r the past eight years;
and
WHEREAS, Doctor Sol J. Rocke and his wife Verva have been a part of the Village of Hazel Crest since
1955;and
WHEREAS, afte r twenty years on the Planning and Zoning Board, Doctor Sol J. Rocke was elected
Village President; and
WHEREAS, the Village has grown and developed under Doctor Rocke's stewardship; and
WHEREAS, Doctor Sol J. Rocke has been an ardent campaigner for economic development in the
Village utilizing all known creative incentives to attract and reta in businesses to Hazel Crest; and
WHEREAS, Doctor Sol J. Rocke has been a staunch supporter of the proposed third airport in Peotone;

and
WHEREAS, Doctor Sol J. Rocke has often encouraged parental responsibility as a means to a safe and
orderly community; and
WHEREAS, Doctor Sol J. Rocke has been a true friend and supporter of education, advocating full
funding for our education system; and
WHEREAS, Doctor Sol J. Rocke has seen the population of Hazel Crest g row by eleven percent in a
land locked community of the Chicago Southland; and
WHEREAS, under Doctor Rocke's leadership, great building has occurred in the Village of Hazel Crest,
including the construction of the Dynasty Lakes Subdivision (Phase I through IV), the Carriage Hil ls
Subdivision, the South Creek Subdivision, Ridgewood Estates, T he C lub, Bank Financial, Mi-Jack
expansion, Full Gospel Church, the Hoekstra Building, the Palmer Lake Venture Building, Stonecreek
Development, G raycor add ition, Arden Courts, Walg reen's, Wendy ' s and South Suburban Hospital
expansion; and
WHEREAS, Doctor Rocke has supported law enforcement through the formation of the multijurisdictional task fo rce, expanding the scope of the local adj udicati on system, advocating the acq uisition
of "N iro" the Village Police dog, authorizing the requisition of a speed trailer to curb vehicular speeding
and by providing full s upport to the Hazel Crest Police Department in becoming an accredited agency;
and
WHEREAS, Doctor Rocke has s upported numerous public improvements in the Vil lage including alley
paving, expansion of the street lig ht system and improvements to public buildings.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the
Board does hereby recognize Doctor Sol J. Rocke for his years of service with the Village of Hazel Crest
and wish him the best of luck during his retirement; and

FRANK A. SPENCER
WHEREAS, Frank A. Spencer was the beloved husband of Catherine, loving stepfather of Marcia and

Patricia, dear brother of Mildred, proud grandfather of four step-grandchildren and one step-greatgrandson, and fond uncle of one niece and nephew, and
WHEREAS, Frank A. Spencer was a lifelong Evanston resident and earned his pilot's license while

studying for his undergraduate degree in economics at Northwestern University. He received his degree
in 1936 and later his doctorate in economics and air transportation from Princeton University in 1941.
His aviation career spanned almost every aspect of the industry and he became a widely respected
aviation expert as a Northwestern University professor, and
WHEREAS, Frank A. Spencer served his country during World War II as a member of the Army Air

Transport Command, flying personnel and supplies to Europe and North Africa, and
WHEREAS, Frank A. Spencer became a pilot for Trans World Airl ines after the war, and then spent

most of his fl ying career at American Airlines until his retirement in 1973. In more than three decades of
flying, he piloted a wide variety of aircraft, from DC-3s to 727s to DC- I Os. He also served as a labor
negotiator for the Air Line Pilots Association and wrote extensively on airline labor issues, regulatory
reform and aviation economics and operations, and
WHEREAS, Frank A. Spencer's distinguished teaching career began when he was appointed to the
faculty of Northwestern University's Kellogg Graduate School of Management in 1973, where he taught
courses in collective bargaining, transportation policy and management. He was appointed to the
Northwestern University Transportation Center in 1978 and became a professor emeritus in 1983,
retaining an office at the center for the remainder of his life, and
WHEREAS, Frank A. Spencer was a benevolent donor to the university. He was instrumental in the
establishment of the William A. Patterson Endowed Chair in Transportation, and
WHEREAS, Frank A. Spencer left an enduring legacy of devotion to his family , educating others, the

pursuit of knowledge, interest in people and ideas, and love of aviation.
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Frank A. Spencer, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his

family in their hour of sorrow and joins his family in honoring his memory, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the fam ily of
Frank A. Spencer as a memorial of his good works and spread upon the offi cial proceedings of this

Honorable Body.

WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called from our midst,
EDNA W. SUMMERS
WHEREAS, Edna W. Summers was the beloved wife of (the late) William, loving mother of Elizabeth,
Stephen and Jerome, dear sister of Robert, proud grandmother of eight grandch ildren, and nine greatgrandchildren, and
WHEREAS, Edna W. Summers was born in Evanston and grad uated in 1938 from Evanston Township
High School. She became a teacher's aide in a Head Start pilot program, a program to increase the school
readiness of children in low-income families, in the mid- I 960s. She became an ardent advocate for the
parents of children to obtain social services for them, which led her to embark on a benevolent, lifelong
career of public service, and
WHEREAS, Edna W. Summers used her enormous talents to help organize the first state Head Start
parent program and to help organize and launch the first federal parent program. She was recognized for
her work as a parent liaison for the Head Start program on the state and national level, and
WHEREAS, Edna W . Summers was a highly respected Evanston alderman who was well versed in
policy issues a nd represented Evanston's 5th Ward on the Evanston City Council for 13 years, beginning
in 1968. She continued her commitment to her community by serving as Evanston Township supervisor
for eight years and as a past president of the Evanston branch of the NAACP, and
WHEREAS, Edna W. Summers demonstrated exceptional civic leadership and unwavering dedication
to improving children's lives, and
WHEREAS, Edna W. Summers was fervently devoted to her family and left an enduring legacy of
passion for her communi ty, faith and devotion, and love for her family.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Edna W. Summers, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to
her fami ly in their hour of sorrow and joins her family in honoring her memory, and

2096

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 5, 200 1

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of thi s Resolution be tendered to the fami ly of
Edna W. Summers as a memorial of her good works and spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 5th day of June 200 I.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County C lerk

WHEREAS, Nereida Aviles represents the epitome of volunteerism, dedicating her heart, her mind, and
her inner strength to the Puerto Rican community of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, born and raised in Vega Baja, Puerto Rico, Nereida moved to the United States in 1954 and
eventually marri ed Felix Aviles; and
WHEREAS, devoted to the strength of fami ly and community values, Nereida and her husband have
presided lovingly over a family of three children and fi ve g randchildren, and they have been good
neighbors and friends to all who have been fortunate enough to know them; and
WHEREAS, Nere ida's selfless dedication to the Puerto Rican community is evident in her every
endeavor whether it's organizing the annual Fiesta Boricua event attended by over I 00,000 people or
coordinating the San Juan Maratho n, the Abrazo, and Three Kings Day; and
WHEREAS, Nereida has become a trusted friend and adv isor to many elected officials, including
Cong ressman Luis Gutierrez for whom she has worked on special projects since 1986 and Alderman Billy
Ocasio for whom she has served as Senio r Advisor since 1993 ; and
WHEREAS, Nereida is a beacon of lig ht for the Puerto Ri can community. Her efforts have not only
earned her the admiration and respect of her colleagues and friends, but have also preserved Puerto Ri can
cultural pride for many generatio ns of fami lies in Cook County.
